<div id="review_418698828" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/418698828" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12248943-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499990463p2/12248943.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/418698828?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/12248943-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=good-ya">good-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=good-books-have-bad-covers">good-books-have-bad-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=third-person">third-person</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=survival">survival</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=aliens">aliens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer418698828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13696799394192089024">Rating: 4.5/5<br/><br/>Wow. I'm finding it hard to walk away from that book with any feelings other than 'impressed'. Also, 'scared as fuck'. I'm not sure if this is the best book of the series so far, because nothing can match the sheer skill of the plotting and writing in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games__1_' title='The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games #1) by Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hunger</a>, but this was certainly the most extreme. Everything about the series - the darkness, the nightmare fuel, the mysteries, the complexity in the plotting - was amped up a notch. Grant's books have always been a pretty unique readi</span>
  <span id="freeText13696799394192089024" style="display:none">Rating: 4.5/5<br /><br />Wow. I'm finding it hard to walk away from that book with any feelings other than 'impressed'. Also, 'scared as fuck'. I'm not sure if this is the best book of the series so far, because nothing can match the sheer skill of the plotting and writing in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games__1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">Hunger</a>, but this was certainly the most extreme. Everything about the series - the darkness, the nightmare fuel, the mysteries, the complexity in the plotting - was amped up a notch. Grant's books have always been a pretty unique reading experience, but this is the book where that stands out the most, where it really comes to the forefront.<br /><br />I do feel compelled to warn you that this book is scarier than before, and it features more 'adult' content. Up until now, a kid as young as ten could probably read the series with no problem, but that's not true anymore. The body horror was so intense that I think a younger kid would be really bothered, when they wouldn't be before. But if you are old enough to read the series, it makes the experience all the better. It's difficult not to be caught up in the intensity of everything, just because there's so much of it. Reading this book becomes a real experience, in a way that the previous books in the series aren't.<br /><br />This shows up in the plotting, in a major way. Grant's pacing is, once again, wonderfully done, so that even when he's weaving four or five different plot threads together, they all feel connected and like they're moving along quickly. Adding to this feeling is the fact that the storyline is genuinely unpredictable, enormously increasing the suspense and the tension. I'm honestly amazed at Grant's ability to create a plot with such a large scope and connect it so effectively and tensely. I don't think I've ever seen anything like this before.<br /><br />Of course, the characterization helps. As with the level of horror, the characterization is amped up a notch, but in a slightly different way. There's a certain bitterness to the characters that wasn't there before. Take Orc for example; I had always found him a bit shallow and uninteresting compared to the others. But this book shows just how depressing and fucked up his life really is, to the point that it's impossible not to feel sorry for him. Or Astrid; this book has her doubting her faith some, which she held onto for so long, and what she does at the end... well, you'll see. (Because you're going to read this series. Whoever you are.) Most of the character arcs that are pushed into the forefront are like this (Dekka, marry me and live on a houseboat), and it's just as impressive as the plotting.<br /><br />The writing, up until now, has been my biggest complaint about the series. It's certainly not bad, it's just been a bit inconsistent. Some scenes are as smooth and effortless as a ballet teacher demonstrating choreography for first graders, others have turns of phrase so obviously awkward that I can't imagine how they survived a single read-though, let alone a long editing process. I'd say that Plague was in the middle in that regard. In the beginning, there was a bit of awkwardness, but it didn't affect anything too much, and by the end of the book, it was completely Gone. (I think I'm going to use that pun in every review of this series that I write...)<br /><br />I wouldn't recommend starting the series with this book, but fans of the series won't be disappointed, and if you're not a fan, then you should definitely remedy that immediately. It's a very strong, well-written series with an almost universal appeal.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13696799394192089024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_158835537" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/158835537" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3086153-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1290873657p2/3086153.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/158835537?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/3086153-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3086153-rachel?shelf=first-reads">first-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158835537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17261498229767918603">I won this as an ARC from Goodreads. <br/><br/>Let me start with saying that I like this series, but I'm not an obsessed fan. I think they're okay and I want to know what's happening, so that might create a little bias on this review. I also get a strange chuckle out of it. Children dying shouldn't be funny... but I laugh. Messed up? Probably. <br/><br/>All the characters are back (at least the ones who haven't died) and the drama is even more dramatic. A plague (duh, read the title) has come and is killing kids wi</span>
  <span id="freeText17261498229767918603" style="display:none">I won this as an ARC from Goodreads. <br /><br />Let me start with saying that I like this series, but I'm not an obsessed fan. I think they're okay and I want to know what's happening, so that might create a little bias on this review. I also get a strange chuckle out of it. Children dying shouldn't be funny... but I laugh. Messed up? Probably. <br /><br />All the characters are back (at least the ones who haven't died) and the drama is even more dramatic. A plague (duh, read the title) has come and is killing kids with a cough so fierce it makes them hack up a lung... literally. To top that off, there are creepy cockroach/wasp like bugs that infest people and eat them from the inside out. And these aren't little bugs you can step on. They're huge and can grow to be the size of Hummers. Ick. I frickin hate bugs. And Drake is back, and now he's indestructible because he was fused with Brittney (read the other books people). So yay, indestructible pysco killer. Plus, they're running out of food (as always) and now water. Canie wants to be king and do Diane, and Sam needs to grow a pair and step up to the plate. And Pete is sick... oh yeah, and Astrid kind of wants to kill him to make the FAZE end. Oh the drama. Here's were I get annoyed. Sam is pissy because in the mist of all the chaos, chaste little Astrid won't do him. Ugh, what a man-ho. And Diana and Caine are just... WHY ARE TEENAGERS SO FREAKING HORMONAL?!?! People are DYING! And all the want to do is SCREW!!! Alright, excuse my language, I had a moment. <br /><br />Let me sum up my feelings before I freak out again. <br />This one wasn't as good as the first two, but I thought it was better paced than the third. Drama, drama, but then again, I kind of thrive off the drama. It's really sick and twisted, but again, I enjoy that about these books. The plot definitely thickens throughout, but it has the same basic lay out. Bad times, getting better, HOPE, but there are bad things and kids are dying, epic battle with Drake/Darkness, drama. That seems to be the sequence for all of them. <br /><br />On a whole, I'm glad I won it and I like it just as well as the others. It gave me a good chuckle and was fast paced enough that I didn't lose interest. I will be reading the rest, because I simply must know what happens.<br /><br />Pretty sure it's released on April 11, so gear up people!<br /><br />3 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="17261498229767918603" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

			<a class="actionLink" href="/topic/show/809794-if-you-were-in-the-fayz-what-would-your-power-be-and-how-many-bars-woul">If you were in the FAYZ, what would your power be and how many bars would it have?</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NPs2Z7oydnK2WDKxbz/TaVXXHLmAQ8D/hsoKE7uIOuGDu2XsfaOnDXrDP462BrM8fjlqYIgkAi0hWKZ4qC1jVw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WkGm0ng7AUMb3ujTgcVmlHdMs1Z4sgMtzUeqC5o1+TbtAfVZv6rQPNdF5exY/AbBXKLFj3DVwf9q1QZgiZCggA==')})
  }
